data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" />76%</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr style="background-color: #eee"><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><div style="text-align: left;">Sources: Passenger Traffic, ACI Europe<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><br /><a href="/wiki/Aeronautical_Information_Publication" title="Aeronautical Information Publication">AIP</a> of Hungary<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Budapest Ferenc Liszt International Airport</b><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a>: <i lang="hu">Budapest Liszt Ferenc Nemzetk\xc3\xb6zi Rep\xc3\xbcl\xc5\x91t\xc3\xa9r</i>) (<a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>BUD</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>LHBP</b>), formerly known as <i>Budapest Ferihegy International Airport</i> and still commonly called just <i><b>Ferihegy</b></i>, is the <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a> serving the Hungarian capital city of <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a>, and by far the largest of the country\'s four commercial airports. The airport is located 16 kilometres (9.9&#160;mi) southeast of the center of Budapest (bordering Pest county) and was renamed in 2011 in honour of the most famous Hungarian composer <a href="/wiki/Franz_Liszt" title="Franz Liszt">Franz Liszt</a> (Liszt Ferenc, in Hungarian) on the occasion of the 200th anniversary of his birth.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>It offers international connections primarily within Europe, but also to Africa, to the Middle East, to North America and to the Far East. In 2019, the airport handled 16.2 million passengers.  The airport is the headquarters and primary hub for <a href="/wiki/Wizz_Air" title="Wizz Air">Wizz Air</a> and base for <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> In 2012 it experienced a significant drop in aircraft movements and handled cargo, primarily due to the collapse of <a href="/wiki/Mal%C3%A9v_Hungarian_Airlines" title="Mal\xc3\xa9v Hungarian Airlines">Mal\xc3\xa9v Hungarian Airlines</a> earlier in the year, hence losing a large portion of connecting passengers. It had been the hub for Mal\xc3\xa9v until the airline\'s bankruptcy on 3 February 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReutersSwoop_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReutersSwoop-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2015 North-American and Middle-Eastern carriers announced direct flights to Budapest. In 2018 <a href="/wiki/LOT_Polish_Airlines" title="LOT Polish Airlines">LOT Polish Airlines</a> made Budapest their first hub outside Poland. Nowadays, the Budapest hub of <a href="/wiki/Wizz_Air" title="Wizz Air">Wizz Air</a> is the largest of all with more than 60 destinations.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#Other_facilities"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Other facilities</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Budapest_Ferenc_Liszt_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Originally called <b>Budapest Ferihegy International Airport</b> (<i>Budapest Ferihegy Nemzetk\xc3\xb6zi Rep\xc3\xbcl\xc5\x91t\xc3\xa9r</i>), on 25 March 2011 it was officially renamed Budapest Liszt Ferenc International Airport, in honor of the Hungarian pianist and composer <a href="/wiki/Franz_Liszt" title="Franz Liszt">Franz Liszt</a> (Modern Hungarian: <i>Liszt Ferenc</i>.) Popularly, the airport is still called <b>Ferihegy</b> as before.\n</p><p>Ferihegy is the name of the neighborhood around the airport. The name is derived from that of Ferenc Xav\xc3\xa9r Mayerffy (1776\xe2\x80\x931845), the former owner of an estate who established vineyards and contributed to the development of <a href="/wiki/Viticulture" title="Viticulture">viticulture</a> in Pest-Buda. "Feri" is a diminutive form of Ferenc while "hegy" means hill. In fact, the area is almost totally flat; but originally there was a 147 m high sandy hillock which was leveled in the 1940s during the construction work of the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Budapest_Ferenc_Liszt_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span id="Designing_and_construction_.281939.E2.80.931944.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Designing_and_construction_(1939\xe2\x80\x931944)">Designing and construction (1939\xe2\x80\x931944)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Budapest_Ferenc_Liszt_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Designing and construction (1939\xe2\x80\x931944)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 1938, the idea of building a new airport in Budapest was born. The area in the boundary of three settlements (Pestszentl\xc5\x91rinc, R\xc3\xa1koshegy and Vecs\xc3\xa9s) was assigned as the area of the new airport. The airport was intended as jointly for civil-military-sporting purposes. Civil facilities were to be built up in the north-western and military ones in the south-western section. Just as for each building, a public tender was invited for the designing and construction of the traffic building.\n<sup id="cite_ref-auto_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In December 1939, upon an announcement of the results of the tender invited in September that year, the designs of K\xc3\xa1roly D\xc3\xa1vid Jr. (1903\xe2\x80\x931973) were chosen. The designer, who was one of the originators of modern Hungarian architectural art, dreamt of a building which resembled an aircraft from the top-side view. The work commenced in 1942. To approach the airport from the city, a 16-kilometre (10&#160;mi) high-speed road was constructed between 1940 and 1943, which, after improvements, remains in use today.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The military buildings were constructed parallel to the civil construction from 1940 but, due to the war situation, faster. Aviation started at the airport in 1943. In wartime, the civil construction slowed down and then stopped at the beginning of 1944. Towards the end of World War II, many of the airport buildings were damaged. By the end 1944, Budapest and its airport were under Soviet occupation.\n<sup id="cite_ref-auto_7-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Reconstruction_.281947.E2.80.931950.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Reconstruction_(1947\xe2\x80\x931950)">Reconstruction (1947\xe2\x80\x931950)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Budapest_Ferenc_Liszt_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Reconstruction (1947\xe2\x80\x931950)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 1947, it was decided that the airport would be reconstructed for civil aviation. Under the three-year plan, 40 million forints were voted for those works. The opening ceremony was held in May 1950 and the sections finished allowed Magyar-Szovjet Polg\xc3\xa1ri L\xc3\xa9giforgalmi Rt. (Hungarian-Soviet Civil Aviation Co. Ltd. \xe2\x80\x93 MASZOVLET), established in 1946, to operate here. At that time the airlines operated only a few foreign flights, in particular, those to <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bucharest" title="Bucharest">Bucharest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sofia" title="Sofia">Sofia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_7-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Magyar L\xc3\xa9giforgalmi V\xc3\xa1llalat (Hungarian Airlines \xe2\x80\x93 Mal\xc3\xa9v) was established on 25 November 1954. The first regular flight taking off from the airport to the West was the Mal\xc3\xa9v\'s flight into Vienna in summer 1956. The first Western airline which launched a flight to Budapest was KLM Royal Dutch Airlines in 1957. The traffic building was finished in this period and the lengthening works of the 2,500-metre (8,202&#160;ft) runway were started. At the end of 1958 the runway was lengthened to 3,010 metres (9,875&#160;ft) and taxiway D was finished.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_7-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Continued_growth_.281960.E2.80.931980.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Continued_growth_(1960\xe2\x80\x931980)">Continued growth (1960\xe2\x80\x931980)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Budapest_Ferenc_Liszt_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Continued growth (1960\xe2\x80\x931980)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ferihegyi_(ma_Liszt_Ferenc)_rep%C3%BCl%C5%91t%C3%A9r,_v%C3%A1r%C3%B3csarnok._Fortepan_84663.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Ferihegyi_%28ma_Liszt_Ferenc%29_rep%C3%BCl%C5%91t%C3%A9r%2C_v%C3%A1r%C3%B3csarnok._Fortepan_84663.jpg/220px-Ferihegyi_%28ma_Liszt_Ferenc%29_rep%C3%BCl%C5%91t%C3%A9r%2C_v%C3%A1r%C3%B3csarnok._Fortepan_84663.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Ferihegyi_%28ma_Liszt_Ferenc%29_rep%C3%BCl%C5%91t%C3%A9r%2C_v%C3%A1r%C3%B3csarnok._Fortepan_84663.jpg/330px-Ferihegyi_%28ma_Liszt_Ferenc%29_rep%C3%BCl%C5%91t%C3%A9r%2C_v%C3%A1r%C3%B3csarnok._Fortepan_84663.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Ferihegyi_%28ma_Liszt_Ferenc%29_rep%C3%BCl%C5%91t%C3%A9r%2C_v%C3%A1r%C3%B3csarnok._Fortepan_84663.jpg/440px-Ferihegyi_%28ma_Liszt_Ferenc%29_rep%C3%BCl%C5%91t%C3%A9r%2C_v%C3%A1r%C3%B3csarnok._Fortepan_84663.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5693" data-file-height="3995" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ferihegyi_(ma_Liszt_Ferenc)_rep%C3%BCl%C5%91t%C3%A9r,_v%C3%A1r%C3%B3csarnok._Fortepan_84663.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Budapest Airport in 1961</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hungary,_Budapest_XVIII._Fortepan_7705.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Hungary%2C_Budapest_XVIII._Fortepan_7705.jpg/220px-Hungary%2C_Budapest_XVIII._Fortepan_7705.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Hungary%2C_Budapest_XVIII._Fortepan_7705.jpg/330px-Hungary%2C_Budapest_XVIII._Fortepan_7705.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Hungary%2C_Budapest_XVIII._Fortepan_7705.jpg/440px-Hungary%2C_Budapest_XVIII._Fortepan_7705.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5437" data-file-height="3645" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hungary,_Budapest_XVIII._Fortepan_7705.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Budapest Airport in 1966</div></div></div>\n<p>Between its opening and 1960, the number of landings at the Airport increased from 4,786 to 17,133, with passenger traffic increasing from 49,955 to 359,338 by 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_7-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1965, a study was made on the development of the airport, which was implemented with more than a 10-year delay from the end of the 1970s. Aviation, airport, and flight control all called for more capacity and infrastructure. The Aviation and Airport Directorate (LRI) was established on 1 January 1973 and performed as an airline company, a trading company, and an authority, as well as investment, operator, and air navigation tasks.\n</p><p>In 1974, passenger traffic reached one million. In 1977, a new control tower was built, as well as a second runway parallel to the old one and a technical base for maintaining MAL\xc3\x89V aircraft. Use of the new 3,707-metre (12,162&#160;ft) runway was started in September 1983.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_7-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="New_infrastructure_.281980.E2.80.932000.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="New_infrastructure_(1980\xe2\x80\x932000)">New infrastructure (1980\xe2\x80\x932000)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Budapest_Ferenc_Liszt_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: New infrastructure (1980\xe2\x80\x932000)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:B762ER_Malev.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/B762ER_Malev.jpg/220px-B762ER_Malev.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/B762ER_Malev.jpg/330px-B762ER_Malev.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/B762ER_Malev.jpg/440px-B762ER_Malev.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:B762ER_Malev.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Boeing_767-200ER" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 767-200ER">Boeing 767-200ER</a> of former flag carrier <a href="/wiki/Mal%C3%A9v_Hungarian_Airlines" title="Mal\xc3\xa9v Hungarian Airlines">Mal\xc3\xa9v Hungarian Airlines</a> at the airport in 2008</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1980, the number of landing aircraft and passengers served reached 32,642 and 1,780,000, respectively. The growing number of passengers called for more capacity. A new terminal was decided upon. The foundation-stone of the new passenger traffic building to be built was laid down on 16 November 1983.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Since 1 November 1985, passengers have been received in Terminal 2, a 24,000-square-meter facility funded with Austrian loans under general contracting. It was used first by Mal\xc3\xa9v aircraft and passengers, and then by those of Lufthansa, Air France, and Swissair. The old terminal continued to receive residual airline traffic under a new name, Terminal 1.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>There was an <a href="/wiki/Improvised_explosive_device" title="Improvised explosive device">IED</a> bus attack against Russian Jewish emigrants on the road leading to Ferihegy in the early 1990s. The perpetrators were members of the German Communist organisation <a href="/wiki/Red_Army_Faction" title="Red Army Faction">Red Army Faction</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1993, Mal\xc3\xa9v launched the airport\'s first Hungarian overseas flight, to New York. According to the traffic figures forecast for the millennium, the two terminals serving 4 million passengers a year promised to be insufficient.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The construction of Terminal 2B was started in 1997. The new building, with more than 30,000 square meters of space, together with a new apron, was opened in 1998, with all foreign airlines moving there. Terminal 2B can receive 3.5 million passengers a year, with its seven gates and five remote stands.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Public_to_public-private_ownership_.282000.E2.80.932012.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_to_public-private_ownership_(2000\xe2\x80\x932012)">Public to public-private ownership (2000\xe2\x80\x932012)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Budapest_Ferenc_Liszt_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Public to public-private ownership (2000\xe2\x80\x932012)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ferihegy2_rep%C3%BCl%C5%91g%C3%A9p-%C3%A1ll%C3%A1sok.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Ferihegy2_rep%C3%BCl%C5%91g%C3%A9p-%C3%A1ll%C3%A1sok.jpg/220px-Ferihegy2_rep%C3%BCl%C5%91g%C3%A9p-%C3%A1ll%C3%A1sok.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="104" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Ferihegy2_rep%C3%BCl%C5%91g%C3%A9p-%C3%A1ll%C3%A1sok.jpg/330px-Ferihegy2_rep%C3%BCl%C5%91g%C3%A9p-%C3%A1ll%C3%A1sok.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Ferihegy2_rep%C3%BCl%C5%91g%C3%A9p-%C3%A1ll%C3%A1sok.jpg/440px-Ferihegy2_rep%C3%BCl%C5%91g%C3%A9p-%C3%A1ll%C3%A1sok.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="283" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ferihegy2_rep%C3%BCl%C5%91g%C3%A9p-%C3%A1ll%C3%A1sok.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Terminal 2 in 2008, prior to the construction of the <i>Sky Court</i></div></div></div>\n<p>On 8 December 2005, a 75% stake in Ferihegy Airport was bought by BAA plc for 464.5 billion HUF (approx. US$2.1 billion), including the right of operation for 75 years.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\nOn 20 October 2006, BAA announced intentions to sell its stake in Budapest Airport to a consortium led by the German airport group, HOCHTIEF AirPort GmbH, subject to the consent of the Hungarian State.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>On 18 April 2007, the renovation of Terminal 1 at Ferihegy was awarded Europe\'s most prestigious heritage preservation prize, the Europa Nostra award.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The designers, contractors, builders and investors (the latter being BA) received the joint award of the European Commission and of the pan-European heritage preservation organisation Europa Nostra for the renovation of the protected monument spaces, the central hall, the gallery and the furniture at T1.\n</p><p>On 6 June 2007, BAA and a consortium led by HOCHTIEF AirPort (HTA) formally closed and completed the transaction of the sale of BAA\'s shares in Budapest Airport (BA) to the HOCHTIEF AirPort Consortium. The ownership of the HOCHTIEF AirPort Consortium was as follows: HOCHTIEF AirPort (49.666%) and three financial investors: Caisse de d\xc3\xa9p\xc3\xb4t et placement du Qu\xc3\xa9bec, Montreal (23.167%), GIC Special Investments, Singapore (23.167%) and KfW IPEX-Bank, Frankfurt (4.0%).<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 26 July 2010, after completing a security oversight investigation in May,<sup id="cite_ref-eubusiness_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eubusiness-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> the EU authorities revoked Budapest Airport\'s official "Schengen Clear" certification, due to serious lapses observed in personal security check procedures and unauthorised passing of banned objects. This meant passenger connecting via another airport in the Schengen Zone would have to be rescreened through security, just as foreign non-Schengen connecting passengers, causing delays and inconvenience. The airport argued that it had not yet had time to fully implement new security measures introduced on 29 April 2010, and inspired by the <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a>\' Amsterdam "underwear bomb scare" incident. The airport\'s layout was also cited as an excuse for the failure. Budapest Airport was the first airport to be checked through a stringent undercover evaluation for compliance with the new regulation. (Hungarian state news agency MTI reports: <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://hirek.mti.hu/english/article/491952/">[1]</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template"><span style="white-space: nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Link_rot" title="Wikipedia:Link rot"><span title="&#160;Dead link since July 2017">permanent dead link</span></a></i>&#93;</span></sup>) In response, additional security measures were immediately implemented at Budapest Airport causing flight delays at both terminals. Unusually long passenger waiting queues were observed at the busier 2A-B terminal complex\'s departures area. These problems were solved over time, especially through the opening of the SkyCourt terminal including a central security zone.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>On 15 November 2010, Budapest Airport regained the "Schengen Clear"-status, after implementing the necessary security actions and after that, the airport underwent the strict re-inspection.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 16 March 2011, the name of Budapest Ferihegy International Airport was changed to Budapest Ferenc Liszt International Airport.[2]\n</p><p>Sky Court, the new expansion project including shops, restaurants and lounges, also connecting Terminals 2A and 2B was opened on 27 March 2011. In summer that year, the refurbishing of the old terminal parts in T2 began and was completed in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Collapse_of_Mal.C3.A9v_and_aftermath_.282012.E2.80.93.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Collapse_of_Mal\xc3\xa9v_and_aftermath_(2012\xe2\x80\x93)">Collapse of Mal\xc3\xa9v and aftermath (2012\xe2\x80\x93)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Budapest_Ferenc_Liszt_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Collapse of Mal\xc3\xa9v and aftermath (2012\xe2\x80\x93)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In the wake of the collapse of <a href="/wiki/Mal%C3%A9v" class="mw-redirect" title="Mal\xc3\xa9v">Mal\xc3\xa9v</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a> announced that it would expand its flights to Liszt airport. Ryanair began selling the flight tickets to the public, but Budapest airport said that the company had not secured all of the necessary slots (which was later negotiated successfully).<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> By 9 February 2012, only six days after the collapse of the Hungarian national carrier, Liszt Ferenc Airport had recovered over 60% of its point to point traffic. Airlines that announced that new services would begin included <a href="/wiki/Wizz_Air" title="Wizz Air">Wizz Air</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Airlines" title="Aegean Airlines">Aegean Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_Berlin" title="Air Berlin">Air Berlin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a>.\n</p><p>However, the airport had lost Mal\xc3\xa9v\'s transfer passengers, which, prior to the airline\'s collapse, had amounted to 1.5 million passengers per year. A second effect of the Mal\xc3\xa9v collapse was that the areas used to service the Mal\xc3\xa9v fleet would no longer generate revenue even once point to point traffic had been restored. These factors created significant financial shortfalls in the airport\'s revenues.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In February 2012, <a href="/wiki/Hainan_Airlines" title="Hainan Airlines">Hainan Airlines</a> announced that they would cease services to Beijing from Budapest.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Prior to the collapse of Mal\xc3\xa9v, Hainan had a partnership with Mal\xc3\xa9v,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> which included a codeshare.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In May 2013, Hochtief Group announced the sale of its Airports unit HOCHTIEF AirPort which held a stake in the Budapest Airport and other airports to the Canadian Pension fund Public Sector Pension Investment Board (PSP Investments).<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Following the sale HOCHTIEF AirPort was renamed AviAlliance.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>From June 2015, <a href="/wiki/Transatlantic_flight" title="Transatlantic flight">transatlantic flights</a> were restored with two carriers flying to Toronto and Montreal.\n</p><p>As of July 2015, the ownership of Budapest Airport is as follows: AviAlliance (52.666%) owned by PSP Investments, Canada, Malton Investment (22.167%) owned by GIC Special Investments, Singapore, Caisse de d\xc3\xa9p\xc3\xb4t et placement du Qu\xc3\xa9bec, Canada (20.167%) and KfW IPEX-Bank, Germany (5%).<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Latest_developments.2C_opening_of_LOT_Polish_Airlines.E2.80.99_base"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Latest_developments,_opening_of_LOT_Polish_Airlines\xe2\x80\x99_base">Latest developments, opening of LOT Polish Airlines\xe2\x80\x99 base</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Budapest_Ferenc_Liszt_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Latest developments, opening of LOT Polish Airlines\xe2\x80\x99 base">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Budapest_Airport-201402.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Budapest_Airport-201402.jpg/220px-Budapest_Airport-201402.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Budapest_Airport-201402.jpg/330px-Budapest_Airport-201402.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Budapest_Airport-201402.jpg/440px-Budapest_Airport-201402.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Budapest_Airport-201402.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Sky Court</i>, the connection building between Terminals 2A and 2B which now houses the main departures waiting hall and shopping area</div></div></div>\n<p>An expenditure of 261 million euros was spent in order to expanding and modernising the airports infrastructure until December 2012. Several of these future projects involve about further 300 million euros, and depends on regulatory decisions as well as third-party investors.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Since 2011, several projects have been completed, including the refurbishment of Terminals 2A and 2B including the inauguration of the <i>Skycourt</i> main departures hall in 2012 and an extension of Terminal 2B in 2018,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> the construction of a new business and cargo area called <i>Budapest Airport Business Park</i><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> as well as a new airport hotel<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> and expanded car parking facilities.\n</p><p>In 2014 <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates</a> opened daily flights to Dubai, UAE using the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777-300ER" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 777-300ER">Boeing 777-300ER</a> aircraft. It was followed by <a href="/wiki/Air_China" title="Air China">Air China</a>\'s flights to <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Capital" class="mw-redirect" title="Beijing Capital">Beijing Capital</a> and an <a href="/wiki/Air_Transat" title="Air Transat">Air Transat</a> connection to <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Pearson" class="mw-redirect" title="Toronto Pearson">Toronto Pearson</a>, both using the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A330" title="Airbus A330">Airbus A330</a>. As a response to that <a href="/wiki/Air_Canada" title="Air Canada">Air Canada</a> started their operation to Budapest by <a href="/wiki/Air_Canada_Rouge" title="Air Canada Rouge">Air Canada Rouge</a> operated by the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_767-300" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 767-300">Boeing 767-300</a>. By 2017 <a href="/wiki/Air_Canada_Rouge" title="Air Canada Rouge">Air Canada Rouge</a> has taken over the market completely.\n</p><p>In July 2017, <a href="/wiki/LOT_Polish_Airlines" title="LOT Polish Airlines">LOT Polish Airlines</a> announced the commencement of direct flights to <a href="/wiki/O%27Hare_International_Airport" title="O&#39;Hare International Airport">Chicago</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">New York</a>, making them the first flights to the United States since <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta</a> and <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a> stopped flying to Budapest in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> New York is served four times, Chicago twice a week with LOT\'s flagship <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787_Dreamliner" title="Boeing 787 Dreamliner">Boeing 787 Dreamliner</a>. In the same year the airline added connections to <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w_John_Paul_II_International_Airport" title="Krak\xc3\xb3w John Paul II International Airport">Krak\xc3\xb3w</a> and <a href="/wiki/London_City_Airport" title="London City Airport">London\xe2\x80\x93City</a>. Right after LOT, <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a> announced their seasonal new flight to <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Philadelphia Airport">Philadelphia Airport</a> which is operated by their <a href="/wiki/Boeing_767" title="Boeing 767">Boeing 767</a> aircraft. In 2020 the airline opens their new route to <a href="/wiki/O%27Hare_International_Airport" title="O&#39;Hare International Airport">Chicago</a> with <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787_Dreamliner" title="Boeing 787 Dreamliner">Boeing 787 Dreamliner</a>. In 2019 <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Airlines" title="Shanghai Airlines">Shanghai Airlines</a> launched a four-time weekly service to <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Pudong_International_Airport" title="Shanghai Pudong International Airport">Shanghai\xe2\x80\x93Pudong</a> also with <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787_Dreamliner" title="Boeing 787 Dreamliner">Boeing 787 Dreamliner</a>. In 2019 <a href="/wiki/LOT_Polish_Airlines" title="LOT Polish Airlines">LOT Polish Airlines</a> announced a massive expansion program with new flights to <a href="/wiki/Belgrade_Nikola_Tesla_Airport" title="Belgrade Nikola Tesla Airport">Belgrade</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Airport" title="Brussels Airport">Brussels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henri_Coand%C4%83_International_Airport" title="Henri Coand\xc4\x83 International Airport">Bucharest</a>, <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A1clav_Havel_Airport_Prague" title="V\xc3\xa1clav Havel Airport Prague">Prague</a>, <a href="/wiki/Incheon_International_Airport" title="Incheon International Airport">Seoul\xe2\x80\x93Incheon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Airport" title="Stuttgart Airport">Stuttgart</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sofia_Airport" title="Sofia Airport">Sofia</a>. The flights will be operated by the airline\'s <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787_Dreamliner" title="Boeing 787 Dreamliner">Boeing 787 Dreamliner</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Embraer_E-Jet_family" title="Embraer E-Jet family">Embraer E-Jet family</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Future">Future</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Budapest_Ferenc_Liszt_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Future">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>There are further projects for the expansion of the airport, including a new cargo facilities area as well as a new Terminal 3,<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> formerly called Terminal 2C which is planned to be finished next to Terminal 2A by 2021.\n</p><p>In 2020, according to a report from bloomberg it was reported that the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Hungary" title="Government of Hungary">Hungarian government</a> was looking at buying the airport from its foreign owners such as <a href="/wiki/GIC_(Singaporean_sovereign_wealth_fund)" title="GIC (Singaporean sovereign wealth fund)">GIC (Singaporean sovereign wealth fund)</a> and Canadian <a href="/wiki/AviAlliance" title="AviAlliance">AviAlliance</a>. Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Orb%C3%A1n" title="Viktor Orb\xc3\xa1n">Viktor Orb\xc3\xa1n</a> was opposed to the 2005 privatization.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminals">Terminals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Budapest_Ferenc_Liszt_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Terminals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Budapest_Ferihegy_2A_LHBP.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Budapest_Ferihegy_2A_LHBP.JPG/220px-Budapest_Ferihegy_2A_LHBP.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Budapest_Ferihegy_2A_LHBP.JPG/330px-Budapest_Ferihegy_2A_LHBP.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Budapest_Ferihegy_2A_LHBP.JPG/440px-Budapest_Ferihegy_2A_LHBP.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Budapest_Ferihegy_2A_LHBP.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Terminal 2A</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FerihegyDep.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/FerihegyDep.jpg/220px-FerihegyDep.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/FerihegyDep.jpg/330px-FerihegyDep.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/FerihegyDep.jpg/440px-FerihegyDep.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="750" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FerihegyDep.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Terminal 2B check-in area</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Liszt_Ferenc_Repuloter_2-es_terminal_varocsarnok_06.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Liszt_Ferenc_Repuloter_2-es_terminal_varocsarnok_06.JPG/220px-Liszt_Ferenc_Repuloter_2-es_terminal_varocsarnok_06.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Liszt_Ferenc_Repuloter_2-es_terminal_varocsarnok_06.JPG/330px-Liszt_Ferenc_Repuloter_2-es_terminal_varocsarnok_06.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Liszt_Ferenc_Repuloter_2-es_terminal_varocsarnok_06.JPG/440px-Liszt_Ferenc_Repuloter_2-es_terminal_varocsarnok_06.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2896" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Liszt_Ferenc_Repuloter_2-es_terminal_varocsarnok_06.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Waiting area <i>Sky Court</i></div></div></div>\n<p>The airport\'s passenger buildings consist of four main areas:\n</p>\n<ul><li><b>Terminal 1</b> is only used for charter and private flights</li>\n<li><b>Terminal 2A</b> is used for flights inside the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a></li>\n<li><b>Terminal 2B</b> is used for flights outside the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a></li>\n<li><b>Sky Court</b>, a large central waiting and shopping area, also the connection of Terminals 2A and 2B</li></ul>\n<h3><span id="Terminal_1_.28closed.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_1_(closed)">Terminal 1 (closed)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Budapest_Ferenc_Liszt_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Terminal 1 (closed)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>From 1 September 2005, re-opened Terminal 1 served low-cost carriers. Terminal 1 is divided into <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen</a> and Non-Schengen boarding gates.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Being located within the premises of Budapest, it offers faster public transport time to the city center, compared to the Terminal 2 about 3 kilometres farther. (Terminal 1 offers an about 20 minutes direct train journey to Budapest city center, while Terminal 2 requires an 8-minute bus ride to the train station).<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 14 March 2012, Budapest Airport announced that due to the traffic levels being too low in Terminal 1, extra capacity in Terminal 2, and cost saving, Terminal 1 will be closed temporarily. On 30 May 2012 all airlines were moved to Terminal 2, the low-cost airlines using now the check-in desks at hall 2B and gates at a makeshift shed outside the main building. This shed now does not operate, a new pier was opened instead.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sky_Court_between_Terminal_2A_and_2B">Sky Court between Terminal 2A and 2B</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Budapest_Ferenc_Liszt_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Sky Court between Terminal 2A and 2B">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Sky Court is a state-of-the-art building between terminals 2A and 2B with 5 levels. Passenger safety checks were moved here along with new baggage classifiers and business class lounges, such as the first MasterCard lounge in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> New shops, restaurants and caf\xc3\xa9s were placed in the new building\'s transit hall. With the opening of Skycourt the Terminal 2 has become capable of receiving about 11 million passengers a year, instead of the former joint capacity of about 7 million.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_2A">Terminal 2A</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Budapest_Ferenc_Liszt_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Terminal 2A">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Schengen terminal, and formerly the "only" Terminal 2. It was inaugurated on 1 November 1985 for the exclusive use of the homeland carrier <a href="/wiki/Mal%C3%A9v_Hungarian_Airlines" title="Mal\xc3\xa9v Hungarian Airlines">Mal\xc3\xa9v Hungarian Airlines</a>, and later renamed in 1998 to Terminal 2A. Its check-in hall serves all Skyteam and Star Alliance member airlines currently. Within its boarding area (Gates A1-A33) and arrivals level, it serves all flights to and from the Schengen-zone destinations of any airline.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_2B">Terminal 2B</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Budapest_Ferenc_Liszt_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Terminal 2B">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The non-Schengen terminal, it is referred to as a separate object, opened in December 1998. Its check-in hall serves all flights of the OneWorld-alliance (intra- and extra-Schengen as well), as well as many other non-aligned airlines. For flights of the Hungarian low-cost airliner <a href="/wiki/Wizz_Air" title="Wizz Air">Wizz Air</a> check-in desks can also be found at this terminal. However, its boarding (Gates B1-B44) and arriving area serve exclusively non-Schengen destinations.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Pier_2B">Pier 2B</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Budapest_Ferenc_Liszt_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Pier 2B">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The project "Pier B" was started on 9 January 2017. The new state-of-the-art building was opened on 1 August 2018, and it is connected directly to Terminal 2B. It is 220 meters long and it includes 27 boarding gates and 10 jetbridges, which can serve more wide-body aircraft at the same time. The pier was planned to offer flexibility for traditional and low-cost airlines with boarding options via jetbridges, buses or walking directly to the aircraft.\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Airlines_and_destinations">Airlines and destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Budapest_Ferenc_Liszt_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Airlines and destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Passenger">Passenger</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Budapest_Ferenc_Liszt_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Passenger">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The following airlines operate regular scheduled and charter services to and from Budapest Ferenc Liszt Airport:<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" style="font-size:95%"><tbody><tr><th>Airlines</th><th International Airport">Athens</a>\n</td></tr><tr><td> <a href="/wiki/Aer_Lingus" title="Aer Lingus">Aer Lingus</a> </td><td> <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Airport" title="Dublin Airport">Madrid</a>\n</td></tr><tr><td> <a href="/wiki/Jet2.com" title="Jet2.com">Jet2.com</a> </td><td> <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_Airport" title="Birmingham Airport">Birmingham</a>, <a class="mw-headline" id="Other_facilities">Other facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Budapest_Ferenc_Liszt_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Other facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Wizz_Air" title="Wizz Air">Wizz Air</a> has its head office in Building 221.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Wizz Air signed the lease agreement in October 2010 and moved there in June 2011 with 150 employees. The airline occupies over 2,000 square metres (22,000&#160;sq&#160;ft) of space in an office building refurbished after the airline\'s arrival. The facility, with open plan offices, houses about 150 employees.<sup id="cite_ref-AirportHQ_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AirportHQ-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> In addition, <a href="/wiki/Farnair_Hungary" class="mw-redirect" title="Farnair Hungary">Farnair Hungary</a> has its head office on the airport property.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mal%C3%A9v_Hungarian_Airlines" title="Mal\xc3\xa9v Hungarian Airlines">Mal\xc3\xa9v Hungarian Airlines</a> signed a lease agreement with the airport in the spring of 2011, agreeing to relocate its headquarters to the airport grounds by the summer of 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-AirportHQ_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AirportHQ-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Due to the collapse of the airline, in February 2012 the plans to move to Ferenc Liszt were cancelled.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ground_transportation">Ground transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Budapest_Ferenc_Liszt_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Ground transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transport">Public transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Budapest_Ferenc_Liszt_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Public transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:100E_busz_(NCA-462).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/100E_busz_%28NCA-462%29.jpg/220px-100E_busz_%28NCA-462%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/100E_busz_%28NCA-462%29.jpg/330px-100E_busz_%28NCA-462%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/100E_busz_%28NCA-462%29.jpg/440px-100E_busz_%28NCA-462%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2747" data-file-height="1791" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:100E_busz_(NCA-462).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bus line 100E (bus service to and from the airport and the city center)</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Budapesti_K%C3%B6zleked%C3%A9si_K%C3%B6zpont" title="Budapesti K\xc3\xb6zleked\xc3\xa9si K\xc3\xb6zpont">Budapesti K\xc3\xb6zleked\xc3\xa9si K\xc3\xb6zpont</a> (BKK), the public transit authority for Budapest, operates two major express bus services to the airport: <a href="/wiki/Budapest_bus_route_100E" title="Budapest bus route 100E">100E</a> and \n<a href="/wiki/Budapest_bus_route_200E" title="Budapest bus route 200E">200E</a>. Route 100E\xe2\x80\x94modeled after the OrlyBus and RoissyBus airport bus services in <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>\xe2\x80\x94provides nonstop service to the city center, stopping only at <a href="/wiki/K%C3%A1lvin_t%C3%A9r" title="K\xc3\xa1lvin t\xc3\xa9r">K\xc3\xa1lvin t\xc3\xa9r</a> and <a href="/wiki/De%C3%A1k_Ferenc_t%C3%A9r" title="De\xc3\xa1k Ferenc t\xc3\xa9r">De\xc3\xa1k Ferenc t\xc3\xa9r</a>. Normal tickets and passes cannot be used on this route; a higher-fare ticket must be bought on board.\n</p><p>Bus route 200E provides service from the airport to <a href="/wiki/K%C5%91b%C3%A1nya-Kispest_(Budapest_Metro)" class="mw-redirect" title="K\xc5\x91b\xc3\xa1nya-Kispest (Budapest Metro)">K\xc5\x91b\xc3\xa1nya-Kispest</a> station, the nearest station of the <a href="/wiki/Budapest_Metro" title="Budapest Metro">Budapest Metro</a>. Normal tickets and passes are valid on this route.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxi">Taxi</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Budapest_Ferenc_Liszt_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Taxi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Another way to get to the city center from the airport is to catch a taxi. Cabs are available all day long in front of the terminal buildings.\n</p><p>Budapest Airport\'s official Taxi partner is F\xc5\x91taxi which has a taxi order stand at both arrival site\'s exit (outside the building).<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:200E_busz_(FKU-933)_cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/200E_busz_%28FKU-933%29_cropped.jpg/220px-200E_busz_%28FKU-933%29_cropped.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/200E_busz_%28FKU-933%29_cropped.jpg/330px-200E_busz_%28FKU-933%29_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/200E_busz_%28FKU-933%29_cropped.jpg/440px-200E_busz_%28FKU-933%29_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3656" data-file-height="2564" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:200E_busz_(FKU-933)_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bus 200E (bus service from the airport to the nearest subway station, K\xc3\xb6b\xc3\xa1nya-Kispest)</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail_and_Bus">Rail and Bus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Budapest_Ferenc_Liszt_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Rail and Bus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Hungarian_State_Railways" title="Hungarian State Railways">Hungarian State Railways</a> runs suburban and long-distance services between (the now closed) Terminal 1 and <a href="/wiki/Nyugati_Railway_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Nyugati Railway Station">Nyugati Railway Station</a> in Budapest city center through <a href="/wiki/K%C5%91b%C3%A1nya-Kispest_(Budapest_Metro)" class="mw-redirect" title="K\xc5\x91b\xc3\xa1nya-Kispest (Budapest Metro)">K\xc5\x91b\xc3\xa1nya-Kispest</a>. The trip takes approximately 25 minutes. From Terminal 2 passengers need to take bus <a href="/wiki/Budapest_bus_route_200E" title="Budapest bus route 200E">200E</a> to Ferihegy vas\xc3\xbat\xc3\xa1llom\xc3\xa1s (<a href="/wiki/Ferihegy_railway_station" title="Ferihegy railway station">Ferihegy railway station</a>). Since July 2017 the <a href="/wiki/Budapest_bus_route_100E" title="Budapest bus route 100E">100E</a> shuttle bus service operates between Terminal 2 and De\xc3\xa1k Ferenc t\xc3\xa9r in the city centre for a special fare.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Flixbus" title="Flixbus">Flixbus</a> operates bus lines from the airport to numerous European cities including <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a>, <a href="/wiki/Timi%C8%99oara" title="Timi\xc8\x99oara">Timi\xc8\x99oara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sibiu" title="Sibiu">Sibiu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mini_buses_and_shuttles">Mini buses and shuttles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Budapest_Ferenc_Liszt_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Mini buses and shuttles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Several companies operate airport shuttles taking passengers to any destination in the city. Other shuttles and coach services exist to outlying towns in Hungary, Romania, Slovakia, and Serbia.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Budapest_Ferenc_Liszt_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Hungary" title="List of airports in Hungary">List of airports in Hungary</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Hungary" title="Transport in Hungary">Transport in Hungary</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Aeropark" title="Aeropark">Aeropark</a> aviation museum</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
